	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Carrie Underwood</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American country music singer</div>

<p><b>Carrie Marie Underwood</b> (born March 10, 1983) is an American singer, songwriter, fashion designer and actress. She rose to fame as the winner of the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_4)" title="American Idol (season 4)">fourth season</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> in 2005. Her debut single, "<a href="/wiki/Inside_Your_Heaven" title="Inside Your Heaven">Inside Your Heaven</a>", made her the only country artist to debut at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart and the only solo country artist in the 2000s to have a number-one song on the Hot 100. Her debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Hearts" title="Some Hearts">Some Hearts</a></i>, was released in 2005. Bolstered by the huge <a href="/wiki/Crossover_music" title="Crossover music">crossover</a> success of the singles "<a href="/wiki/Jesus,_Take_the_Wheel" title="Jesus, Take the Wheel">Jesus, Take the Wheel</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Before_He_Cheats" title="Before He Cheats">Before He Cheats</a>", it became the best-selling solo female debut album in country music history, the fastest-selling debut country album in <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> history and the best-selling country album of the last 16 years. Underwood won three <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> for the album, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_New_Artist" title="Grammy Award for Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a>.
</p><p>Her second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Carnival_Ride" title="Carnival Ride">Carnival Ride</a></i>, followed in 2007. It had one of the biggest opening weeks of all time by a female artist and won two Grammy Awards. Her next album, 2009's <i><a href="/wiki/Play_On_(Carrie_Underwood_album)" title="Play On (Carrie Underwood album)">Play On</a></i>, was a commercial success led by the single "<a href="/wiki/Cowboy_Casanova" title="Cowboy Casanova">Cowboy Casanova</a>". Underwood's fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_(album)" title="Blown Away (album)">Blown Away</a></i> (2012), earned her a Grammy Award and was that year's second best-selling release by a female artist. Her first <a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits:_Decade_Number_1" title="Greatest Hits: Decade Number 1">compilation album</a> (2014), a chart and sales success, spawned the Grammy Award-winning crossover single "<a href="/wiki/Something_in_the_Water_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Something in the Water (Carrie Underwood song)">Something in the Water</a>". Her fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Storyteller_(Carrie_Underwood_album)" title="Storyteller (Carrie Underwood album)">Storyteller</a></i> (2015), made her the only country artist to have all first five studio albums reach either numbers one or two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart. With her sixth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Cry_Pretty" title="Cry Pretty">Cry Pretty</a></i> (2018), she became the only woman to top the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with four country albums, and had both the biggest week for any album by a woman in 2018 and the best-selling solo female album of the year.
</p><p>One of the most successful music artists, Underwood has sold 70 million records worldwide. She is the seventh highest-certified female artist of all time on the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>'s Top Artists (Digital Singles) ranking and the highest-certified country album artist to debut in the 21st century. Underwood is also the woman with most number-one singles on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Country_Airplay" title="Country Airplay">Country Airplay</a> chart, with 15. Her <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Carrie_Underwood" title="List of awards and nominations received by Carrie Underwood">awards and accolades</a> include seven <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>, 11 <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard Music Awards"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>, 13 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, a <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Record" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness World Record">Guinness World Record</a></i>, 14 <a href="/wiki/ACM_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="ACM Awards">ACM Awards</a> and nine <a href="/wiki/CMA_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="CMA Awards">CMA Awards</a>. Acclaimed by <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> as "the female vocalist of her generation of any genre", she was listed by <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">one of the 100 most influential people in the world</a> in 2014. <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> has declared her the most successful <i>American Idol</i> winner. <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> named <i>Some Hearts</i> the number-one country album of the 2000s and her as the top female artist on its "Best Country Artists of the 2000s" list. She has been inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ole_Opry" title="Grand Ole Opry">Grand Ole Opry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Hall_of_Fame" title="Oklahoma Hall of Fame">Oklahoma Hall of Fame</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Oklahoma Music Hall of Fame">Oklahoma Music Hall of Fame</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Underwood was born March 10, 1983,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-biography.com_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biography.com-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Muskogee,_Oklahoma" title="Muskogee, Oklahoma">Muskogee, Oklahoma</a>, to Carole (née Shatswell) and Steve Underwood,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> She has two older sisters, Shanna and Stephanie,<sup id="cite_ref-Biography_Today_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biography_Today-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and was raised on her parents' farm in the nearby rural town of <a href="/wiki/Checotah,_Oklahoma" title="Checotah, Oklahoma">Checotah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PeopleBio_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeopleBio-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Her father worked in a <a href="/wiki/Paper_mill" title="Paper mill">paper mill</a> while her mother taught elementary school.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> She was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Attention_deficit_hyperactivity_disorder" title="Attention deficit hyperactivity disorder">attention deficit hyperactivity disorder</a> at age five and was prescribed <a href="/wiki/Ritalin" class="mw-redirect" title="Ritalin">Ritalin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dexedrine" class="mw-redirect" title="Dexedrine">Dexedrine</a>, medicines she still takes as an adult.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> During her childhood, Underwood performed at Robbins Memorial Talent Show, and sang at her local church, First Free Will Baptist Church. She later sang for local events in Checotah, including Old Settler's Day and the <a href="/wiki/Lion%27s_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Lion&#39;s Club">Lion's Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BuddyTV_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BuddyTV-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A local admirer arranged for her to go to <a href="/wiki/Nashville" class="mw-redirect" title="Nashville">Nashville</a> when she was 14 to audition for <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Biography_Today,_p.144_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biography_Today,_p.144-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, Capitol Records was preparing a contract for Underwood but canceled it when company management changed. Underwood said of the event, "I honestly think it's a lot better that nothing came out of it now, because I wouldn't have been ready then. Everything has a way of working out."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While at Checotah High School, she was an Honor Society member, a cheerleader, and played basketball and softball.<sup id="cite_ref-Biography_Today,_p.145_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biography_Today,_p.145-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Underwood graduated from Checotah High School in 2001 as <a href="/wiki/Salutatorian" title="Salutatorian">salutatorian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BuddyTV_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BuddyTV-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> She chose not to pursue singing after graduation. She said, "After high school, I pretty much gave up on the dream of singing. I had reached a point in my life where I had to be practical and prepare for my future in the 'real world'".<sup id="cite_ref-Biography_Today,_p.145_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biography_Today,_p.145-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She attended <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_State_University" title="Northeastern State University">Northeastern State University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tahlequah,_Oklahoma" title="Tahlequah, Oklahoma">Tahlequah, Oklahoma</a>, graduating <i><a href="/wiki/Latin_honors" title="Latin honors">magna cum laude</a></i> in 2006 with a bachelor's degree in <a href="/wiki/Mass_communication" title="Mass communication">mass communication</a> and an emphasis in journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-usatoday_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> She spent part of one of her summers as a page for Oklahoma State Representative Bobby Frame.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> She also waited tables at a pizzeria, worked at a zoo, and at a veterinary clinic.<sup id="cite_ref-Biography_Today,_p.145_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biography_Today,_p.145-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Underwood is an alumna of the Alpha Iota chapter of <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Sigma_Sigma" title="Sigma Sigma Sigma">Sigma Sigma Sigma</a> sorority.<sup id="cite_ref-sigma_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sigma-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For two summers, she performed in Northeastern State University's Downtown Country show in Tahlequah. She competed in numerous beauty pageants at the university and was selected as Miss NSU runner-up in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-pbs_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="2004.E2.80.932005:_American_Idol"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2004–2005:_American_Idol">2004–2005: <i>American Idol</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2004–2005: American Idol">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>In the summer of 2004, Underwood auditioned for <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, singing <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Raitt" title="Bonnie Raitt">Bonnie Raitt</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Make_You_Love_Me" title="I Can&#39;t Make You Love Me">I Can't Make You Love Me</a>". After she sang "<a href="/wiki/Could%27ve_Been_(Tiffany_song)" title="Could&#39;ve Been (Tiffany song)">Could've Been</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_(American_singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiffany (American singer)">Tiffany</a> on the top 12 girls night, judge <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a> commented that she would be one of the favorites to win the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> During the top 11 finalists' performance on the March 22, 2005, <i>Idol</i> episode, Underwood sang a rendition of the number-one 1980s rock hit "<a href="/wiki/Alone_(Heart_song)" title="Alone (Heart song)">Alone</a>", made famous by <a href="/wiki/Heart_(band)" title="Heart (band)">Heart</a>, and Cowell predicted that Underwood would not only win the competition, but she would also outsell all previous <i>Idol</i> winners.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> One of the show's producers later said she dominated the voting, winning every week handily.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> She gained a fan base known as "Carrie's Care Bears" during the course of the show. During the final, she sang with <a href="/wiki/Rascal_Flatts" title="Rascal Flatts">Rascal Flatts</a> on "<a href="/wiki/Bless_the_Broken_Road" title="Bless the Broken Road">Bless the Broken Road</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On May 25, 2005, Underwood became the season four winner. Her winnings included a recording contract worth at least a million dollars, use of a private jet for a year, and a <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a> convertible.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2005.E2.80.932007:_Some_Hearts_and_breakthrough"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005–2007:_Some_Hearts_and_breakthrough">2005–2007: <i>Some Hearts</i> and breakthrough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2005–2007: Some Hearts and breakthrough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg/220px-CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg/330px-CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg/440px-CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1619" data-file-height="2155" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CroppedCarrieUnderwoodAtTheWorldArena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performing at the <a href="/wiki/World_Arena,_Colorado_Springs" class="mw-redirect" title="World Arena, Colorado Springs">World Arena</a> in December 2006</div></div></div>
<p>Underwood's music career began with the release of her first single, "<a href="/wiki/Inside_Your_Heaven" title="Inside Your Heaven">Inside Your Heaven</a>", on June 14, 2005. The song debuted at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, with Underwood becoming only the third artist to bow in the top slot since chart policy changed in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> She also broke <i>Billboard</i> chart history as the first country music artist ever to debut at No. 1 on the Hot 100 and the song became the first song from a country artist to go to No. 1 on the Hot 100 since country group <a href="/wiki/Lonestar" title="Lonestar">Lonestar</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Amazed" title="Amazed">Amazed</a>" did so in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-PRNewswire_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRNewswire-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> "Inside Your Heaven" is the only single by a solo country artist in the decade of 2000–2009 to reach No. 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> It also debuted at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Pop_100" title="Pop 100"><i>Billboard</i> Pop 100</a> and on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Singles_Chart" title="Canadian Singles Chart">Canadian Singles Chart</a>, topping it for seven consecutive weeks, becoming the longest-running single of 2005 in Canada. It sold nearly one million copies and was certified gold by the RIAA and double platinum by the CRIA.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa.com_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa.com-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cert_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cert-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood's debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Hearts" title="Some Hearts">Some Hearts</a></i>, was released on November 15, 2005, entering the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts"><i>Billboard</i> charts</a> with 315,000 copies sold, debuting at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Top_Country_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Country Albums"><i>Billboard</i> Top Country Albums</a> and at No. 2 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The large first week sales of <i>Some Hearts</i> made it the biggest debut of any country artist since the advent of the <a href="/wiki/SoundScan" class="mw-redirect" title="SoundScan">SoundScan</a> system in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <i>Some Hearts</i> became the best-selling album of 2006 in all genres in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The album was also the best-selling country album of both 2006 and 2007, making Underwood the first female artist in <i>Billboard</i> history to earn back-to-back honors for Top Country Album.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, it was the best-selling female country album of 2005, 2006, and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <i>Some Hearts</i> has since become the fastest-selling debut country album in the history of the <a href="/wiki/SoundScan" class="mw-redirect" title="SoundScan">SoundScan</a> era,<sup id="cite_ref-cmt20070110_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmt20070110-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cst_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cst-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> the best-selling solo female debut album in country music history,<sup id="cite_ref-Gactv.com_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gactv.com-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> the best-selling Country album of the last 14 years,<sup id="cite_ref-Grein_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grein-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and the best-selling album by an <i>American Idol</i> alumni in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The album is certified eight times platinum by the RIAA, the highest album certification of any country artist to emerge since 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's second single,<sup id="cite_ref-bullatlanta1_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bullatlanta1-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Jesus,_Take_the_Wheel" title="Jesus, Take the Wheel">Jesus, Take the Wheel</a>" was released to radio in October and later peaked at No. 1 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> Hot Country Songs, topping it for six consecutive weeks, and at number twenty on the Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The song sold over two million copies and was certified double Platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Underwood's third single, "Some Hearts", was also released in October, but exclusively to pop radio. "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Forget_to_Remember_Me" title="Don&#39;t Forget to Remember Me">Don't Forget to Remember Me</a>", her fourth single, also proved successful, reaching No. 2 on the Hot Country Songs chart. Later that autumn, Underwood's third country single,<sup id="cite_ref-bullatlanta1_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bullatlanta1-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Before_He_Cheats" title="Before He Cheats">Before He Cheats</a>", hit No. 1 on <i>Billboard</i>'s Hot Country Songs, staying there for five consecutive weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The song peaked at No. 8 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, achieving the slowest climb ever to the top 10 of the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, breaking the record that was previously held by <a href="/wiki/Creed_(band)" title="Creed (band)">Creed</a> from July 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In February 2008, when it was certified double Platinum, "Before He Cheats" became the first country song to ever be certified multi-platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It has now been certified five times Platinum, selling more than four million copies, and is the fourth best-selling country digital song of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa.com_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa.com-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On April 11, 2007, Underwood continued her streak of top Country singles with the release of "<a href="/wiki/Wasted_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Wasted (Carrie Underwood song)">Wasted</a>", which peaked at No. 1 on the Hot Country Songs chart, sold more than one million copies and was certified Platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1958_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1958-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In August 2008, the "Jesus, Take the Wheel" ringtone was reported to have been certified Platinum, making Underwood the first country artist ever to have two songs hit Platinum Mastertone status together with "Before He Cheats", which had been certified earlier in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Underwood started her first headlined tour, <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood:_Live_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Carrie Underwood: Live 2006">Carrie Underwood: Live 2006</a>, with dates across <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="914" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performing in Iraq, in December 2006</div></div></div>
<p>At the 2005 <i>Billboard</i> Music Awards, her hit song "<a href="/wiki/Inside_Your_Heaven" title="Inside Your Heaven">Inside Your Heaven</a>" won the coveted Top-Selling Hot 100 Song of the Year award and also Top-Selling Country Single of the Year award, and she won Country Single Sales Artist of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> At the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music Awards</a>, she won Top New Female Vocalist and Single of the Year, for "Jesus, Take the Wheel".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> At the 40th Annual <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="Country Music Association Awards">Country Music Association Awards</a>, she won both the Horizon Award (now New Artist of the Year) and Female Vocalist of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> At the 2006 <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Awards</a>, Underwood won both the Breakthrough Video of the Year and Female Video of the Year for "Jesus, Take The Wheel".<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> She later won the Breakthrough Artist of the Year Award at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, and was also nominated for Favorite Female Country Artist.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> She won five awards at the 2006 <i>Billboard</i> Music Awards, including the coveted Album of the Year, Top 200 Female Artist of the Year, Female Country Artist, New Country Artist, and Country Album of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard2006_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2006-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> That year, Underwood also won a <a href="/wiki/GMA_Dove_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="GMA Dove Awards">Gospel Music Association (GMA) Dove Award</a> for Country Recorded Song of the Year, for "Jesus, Take The Wheel".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> Awards in 2007, Underwood won Album of the Year, Video of the Year, and Female Vocalist of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> She was nominated for "World's Best Selling New Artist" at the 2006 <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>. At the 2007 CMT Awards in <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a>, on April 16, Underwood's "Before He Cheats" won three awards, including Video of the Year, Female Video of the Year, and Video Director of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Underwood won two awards at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association" title="Country Music Association">CMA Awards</a>: Female Vocalist of the Year, for the second consecutive time, and Single Record of the Year, for "Before He Cheats".<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, at the <a href="/wiki/49th_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="49th Grammy Awards">49th Grammy Awards</a>, <i>Some Hearts</i> received four <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> nominations and Underwood won her first two Grammy Awards: <a href="/wiki/Best_New_Artist" class="mw-redirect" title="Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Best_Female_Country_Vocal_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Female Country Vocal Performance">Best Female Country Vocal Performance</a> for "Jesus, Take the Wheel.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> By winning the Best New Artist Grammy Award, Underwood became only the second country artist to ever win the award in the 56-year history of the Grammy Awards, following <a href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes" title="LeAnn Rimes">LeAnn Rimes</a> (1997).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> She sang the <a href="/wiki/Eagles_(band)" title="Eagles (band)">Eagles</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Life_in_the_Fast_Lane" title="Life in the Fast Lane">Life in the Fast Lane</a>" alongside Grammy nominees <a href="/wiki/Rascal_Flatts" title="Rascal Flatts">Rascal Flatts</a>. She also sang the Eagles' "<a href="/wiki/Desperado_(Eagles_song)" title="Desperado (Eagles song)">Desperado</a>" to honor <a href="/wiki/Don_Henley" title="Don Henley">Don Henley</a> of The Eagles. She also paid tribute to <a href="/wiki/Bob_Wills_and_His_Texas_Playboys" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Wills and His Texas Playboys">Bob Wills and His Texas Playboys</a> by performing "<a href="/wiki/New_San_Antonio_Rose" title="New San Antonio Rose">New San Antonio Rose</a>". At the <a href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="50th Grammy Awards">50th Grammy Awards</a>, in 2008, Underwood was nominated for two more Grammys: Best Female Country Vocal Performance, for "Before He Cheats" and <a href="/wiki/Best_Country_Collaboration_with_Vocals" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Country Collaboration with Vocals">Best Country Collaboration with Vocals</a>, for "Oh, Love" a duet with <a href="/wiki/Brad_Paisley" title="Brad Paisley">Brad Paisley</a>. She won one Grammy Award that night, for Best Female Country Vocal Performance, and performed the song at the ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2005, Underwood was named Oklahoman of the Year by <i><a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Today_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oklahoma Today (magazine)">Oklahoma Today</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-realitytv_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-realitytv-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In December 2006, Underwood joined <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bubl%C3%A9" title="Michael Bublé">Michael Bublé</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Groban" title="Josh Groban">Josh Groban</a> to sing "<a href="/wiki/For_Once_in_My_Life" title="For Once in My Life">For Once in My Life</a>" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">The Oprah Winfrey Show</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> That same month, she paid tribute to <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>, by singing "<a href="/wiki/Islands_in_the_Stream_(song)" title="Islands in the Stream (song)">Islands in the Stream</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Rogers" title="Kenny Rogers">Kenny Rogers</a> (originally by Parton and Rogers) at the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a>, which honored Parton that year.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Underwood performed with the <a href="/wiki/United_Service_Organizations" title="United Service Organizations">USO</a> Christmas Tour in Iraq during the 2006 Holiday season.<sup id="cite_ref-uso_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uso-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Underwood also performed at the <a href="/wiki/Idol_Gives_Back#Idol_Gives_Back_2007" title="Idol Gives Back">2007 Idol Gives Back</a> concert, singing "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Stand_By_You" class="mw-redirect" title="I&#39;ll Stand By You">I'll Stand By You</a>", a cover of <a href="/wiki/Pretenders_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pretenders (band)">The Pretenders</a> hit. Her version of the song debuted at No. 6 on <i>Billboard</i>'s Hot 100 Songs.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> reported that Underwood earned over $7 million between June 2006 and June 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2007, <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret" title="Victoria&#39;s Secret">Victoria's Secret</a> named Underwood the Sexiest Female Musician.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932009:_Carnival_Ride_and_commercial_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–2009:_Carnival_Ride_and_commercial_success">2007–2009: <i>Carnival Ride</i> and commercial success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2007–2009: Carnival Ride and commercial success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Carrie_Underwood.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Carrie_Underwood.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Carrie_Underwood.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="972" data-file-height="1284" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood at the <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> Experience premiere, February 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Underwood's second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Carnival_Ride" title="Carnival Ride">Carnival Ride</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> was released in October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-msnbc01_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc01-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> On <i>Carnival Ride</i>, Underwood was more involved in the songwriting process; she set up a writers' retreat at Nashville's <a href="/wiki/Ryman_Auditorium" title="Ryman Auditorium">Ryman Auditorium</a> to collaborate with such Music Row tunesmiths as <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Lindsey" title="Hillary Lindsey">Hillary Lindsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Wiseman" title="Craig Wiseman">Craig Wiseman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rivers_Rutherford" title="Rivers Rutherford">Rivers Rutherford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gordie_Sampson" title="Gordie Sampson">Gordie Sampson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> <i>Carnival Ride</i> moved over 527,000 copies in its first week, debuting at No. 1 on both the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and Top Country Albums, as well as No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>, one of the biggest first-week sales by a female artist.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <i>Carnival Ride</i> was certified double platinum in just two months after its release in December.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The album is now certified four times Multi-Platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/So_Small" title="So Small">So Small</a>", the first single from the album, was released in July 2007 and reached No. 1 on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>'s Hot Country Songs, topping it for three consecutive weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-cmt20070731_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmt20070731-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/All-American_Girl_(song)" title="All-American Girl (song)">All-American Girl</a>", the second single, also reached No. 1 on the Hot Country Songs chart. The next single, "<a href="/wiki/Last_Name_(song)" title="Last Name (song)">Last Name</a>", reached No. 1 on the Hot Country Song chart as well. This made Underwood the first female artist to have two consecutive albums each release three number ones on this chart since <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a> in 1998. "<a href="/wiki/Just_a_Dream_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Just a Dream (Carrie Underwood song)">Just a Dream</a>", the album's next single, was released on July 2008 and later peaked at No. 1 on the Hot Country Songs chart, staying there for two consecutive weeks. With that, Underwood became the first solo female artist to pull four number one's from one album since Twain did it with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woman_in_Me_(Shania_Twain_album)" title="The Woman in Me (Shania Twain album)">The Woman in Me</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The album's fifth single, "<a href="/wiki/I_Told_You_So_(Randy_Travis_song)" title="I Told You So (Randy Travis song)">I Told You So</a>", a duet with the original singer of the song, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Travis" title="Randy Travis">Randy Travis</a>, was released in February 2009. It peaked at No. 2 on the Country charts and No. 9 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. All singles from <i>Carnival Ride</i> were certified Platinum by the RIAA, for selling more than one million copies each.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In January 2008, Underwood embarked on a joint tour with <a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a> named the <i>Love, Pain and the Whole Crazy Carnival Ride Tour</i>, with dates fixed nationwide that continued through April.<sup id="cite_ref-crazy_carnival_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crazy_carnival-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> She then started her headlined tour, the Carnival Ride Tour, in February 2008, with dates across all North America, and ended it on December 14, 2008, playing to 1.2 million fans throughout the tour and being named the top-selling country female touring artist of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_(3327953047).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_%283327953047%29.jpg/220px-Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_%283327953047%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_%283327953047%29.jpg/330px-Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_%283327953047%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_%283327953047%29.jpg/440px-Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_%283327953047%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3056" data-file-height="2292" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_underwood...little_big_town_276_(3327953047).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performing during the Carnival Ride Tour, 2007.</div></div></div>
<p>At the end of 2007, Underwood topped five <i>Billboard</i> Year-End charts, including <i>Billboard</i> 200 Artist of the Year and also Country Artist of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Also in late 2007, she won three <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>: Artist of the Year, Favorite Female Country Artist, and Favorite Country Album, for <i>Some Hearts</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> At the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music Awards</a>, she won Female Vocalist of the Year, for the 2nd consecutive time.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> She received two nominations for the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association" title="Country Music Association">Country Music Association</a> Awards. Underwood and Brad Paisley co-hosted the awards show and she walked away with the Female Vocalist of the Year award for the third consecutive time but lost the Album of the Year award to <a href="/wiki/George_Strait" title="George Strait">George Strait</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> At the 2008 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, Carnival Ride won the Favorite Country Album award, thus making that her 2nd consecutive win in such category.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, Underwood won her first international award, which was "Female Vocalist of the Year" at the <a href="/wiki/European_Country_Music_Association" title="European Country Music Association">European Country Music Association</a> Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> For the 44th <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> Awards, in 2009, Underwood was nominated for four major awards. Underwood won for Female Vocalist of the Year and Entertainer of the Year, thus making her the first woman to win the award in ten years and the 7th female to take it in the award show's four-decade run.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Underwood was nominated for Video of the Year at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Television">CMT</a> Awards for "Just A Dream". In 2009, at the <a href="/wiki/51st_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="51st Grammy Awards">51st Grammy Awards</a>, she won, for the third year in a row, the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Country_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Country Vocal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Female Country Vocal Performance</a>, for "Last Name", and performed the song at the ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/52nd_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="52nd Grammy Awards">52nd Grammy Awards</a> in 2010, Underwood won her fifth Grammy Award: She won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Country_Collaboration_with_Vocals" title="Grammy Award for Best Country Collaboration with Vocals">Grammy Award for Best Country Collaboration with Vocals</a> for "<a href="/wiki/I_Told_You_So_(Randy_Travis_song)" title="I Told You So (Randy Travis song)">I Told You So</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Randy_Travis" title="Randy Travis">Randy Travis</a> and was also nominated again for Best Female Country Vocal Performance, for "Just A Dream".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> At the ceremony, she performed with <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Robinson" title="Smokey Robinson">Smokey Robinson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Hudson" title="Jennifer Hudson">Jennifer Hudson</a> during the 3-D <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> tribute.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Grammy Awards producer Ken Ehrlich stated that Michael Jackson greatly admired Underwood, which is why she was hand-picked to perform during his tribute.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 13, 2008, Underwood was invited by <a href="/wiki/Randy_Travis" title="Randy Travis">Randy Travis</a> to become a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Grand_Ole_Opry_Members" title="List of Grand Ole Opry Members">member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ole_Opry" title="Grand Ole Opry">Grand Ole Opry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Later that month she was officially inducted by <a href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks" title="Garth Brooks">Garth Brooks</a> into the Grand Ole Opry.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A few months earlier, she sang <a href="/wiki/Julie_Andrews" title="Julie Andrews">Julie Andrews</a>'s classic, the title song from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music" title="The Sound of Music">The Sound of Music</a></i>, at the 2007 <i>Movies Rock: A Celebration Of Music In Film</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On October 22, 2008, Underwood unveiled her wax figure at <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> New York.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, it was reported by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> that Underwood earned over $9 million between June 2007 and June 2008, being No. 79 on the Top Celebrity 100 list.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes.com_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes.com-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> reported that Underwood was the top earning <i>American Idol</i> alumnus from June 2008 to May 17, 2009. She earned more than twice as much as the second-place finisher, with estimated earnings of $14&#160;million during this time period.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_Earning_Idols_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Earning_Idols-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> She appeared on the holiday CD <i>Hear Something Country Christmas 2007</i> with a rendition of "<a href="/wiki/Do_You_Hear_What_I_Hear%3F" title="Do You Hear What I Hear?">Do You Hear What I Hear?</a>". The song reached No. 2 on the AC Chart and remained there for three consecutive weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> She recorded the song "Ever Ever After" for <a href="/wiki/Enchanted_(soundtrack)" title="Enchanted (soundtrack)">the soundtrack</a> of the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Enchanted_(2007_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Enchanted (2007 film)">Enchanted</a></i>. Underwood co-wrote a song for <i>Idol</i> alum <a href="/wiki/Kristy_Lee_Cook" title="Kristy Lee Cook">Kristy Lee Cook</a>'s major-label debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Why_Wait_(album)" title="Why Wait (album)">Why Wait</a></i>. At the <a href="/wiki/Idol_Gives_Back#Idol_Gives_Back_2008" title="Idol Gives Back">2008 Idol Gives Back</a>, she sang <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>'s classic "<a href="/wiki/Praying_For_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Praying For Time">Praying For Time</a>" and later recorded it.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In November 2008, Underwood recorded a virtual and posthumous duet with <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, on his classic "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_Home_For_Christmas" class="mw-redirect" title="I&#39;ll Be Home For Christmas">I'll Be Home For Christmas</a>", for his 2008 album <i>Christmas Duets</i>. Elvis's ex-wife, <a href="/wiki/Priscilla_Presley" title="Priscilla Presley">Priscilla Presley</a>, herself asked Underwood to do the duet: "Priscilla wanted me to do 'I'll Be Home For Christmas'", she says. "I couldn't say 'no'."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In March 2009, she tracked a cover of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe" title="Mötley Crüe">Mötley Crüe</a>'s ballad "<a href="/wiki/Home_Sweet_Home_(M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe_song)" title="Home Sweet Home (Mötley Crüe song)">Home Sweet Home</a>" for the <i>American Idol</i> <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_8)" title="American Idol (season 8)">season eight</a> farewell theme.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.932012:_Play_On_and_collaborations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–2012:_Play_On_and_collaborations">2009–2012: <i>Play On</i> and collaborations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2009–2012: Play On and collaborations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg/220px-CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg/330px-CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg/440px-CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1654" data-file-height="2001" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CarrieUnderwoodNov09.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a></div></div></div>
<p>Underwood released her third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Play_On_(Carrie_Underwood_album)" title="Play On (Carrie Underwood album)">Play On</a></i>, on November 3, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted atop both the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and Top Country Albums, selling over 318,000 copies in its first week, and became, upon its release, the top-selling release of the year by a female artist, but was later overtaken by <a href="/wiki/Susan_Boyle" title="Susan Boyle">Susan Boyle</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/I_Dreamed_a_Dream_(album)" title="I Dreamed a Dream (album)">I Dreamed a Dream</a></i> and finished the year as No. 2.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Underwood wrote a song with pop/R&amp;B singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a> for the album, the song, however, did not make the album.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The first single from the album, "<a href="/wiki/Cowboy_Casanova" title="Cowboy Casanova">Cowboy Casanova</a>", co-written by Underwood, <a href="/wiki/Brett_James" title="Brett James">Brett James</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Mike_Elizondo" title="Mike Elizondo">Mike Elizondo</a>, was released in September 2009. It was a huge success, jumping from No. 96 to No. 11 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 in its second week, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones#Biggest_single-week_upward_movements" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">biggest single-week upwards on the chart</a> of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> It later peaked at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs">Hot Country Songs</a> chart in just ten weeks, the year's fastest chart-topper by a country female and the fastest number one of her career at that time (her 2014 single "Something in the Water" topped the Hot Country Songs chart in its seventh week).<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> "Cowboy Casanova" has sold over 2 million copies, being certified double Platinum. Second single, "<a href="/wiki/Temporary_Home" title="Temporary Home">Temporary Home</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> hit No. 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Country Songs and the RIAA certified it Platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-theboot.com_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theboot.com-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Undo_It" title="Undo It">Undo It</a>", Underwood's third single from "Play On", was released to radio in May. It was later certified Platinum and hit No. 1 on the Hot Country Songs chart, giving Underwood her tenth number-one single on the Hot Country Songs.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The 4th single from <i>Play On</i>, "<a href="/wiki/Mama%27s_Song" title="Mama&#39;s Song">Mama's Song</a>", was released to country radio in September, peaked at two on the Hot Country Songs and was certified Gold by the RIAA. The album is certified Triple Platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa.com-2_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa.com-2-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood's <a href="/wiki/Play_On_Tour" title="Play On Tour">Play On Tour</a> started its first leg on March 11, 2010, in <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Pennsylvania" title="Reading, Pennsylvania">Reading, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The second leg of the tour started on September 25, 2010, in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>, and ended January 1, 2011, in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Underwood sold out the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Bowl" title="Hollywood Bowl">Hollywood Bowl</a> on October 2, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2010, Pollstar.com ranked the Play On Tour one of the Top 50 tours of 2010, at No. 1 on the North American raking, and No. 31 worldwide. <i>Billboard</i> also ranked Underwood's tour at No. 24 for all worldwide tours of 2010. On January 4, 2011, official statistics revealed that Underwood played to over 1 million fans throughout the tour,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> resulting in her being named again as the top-ranked female country touring artist of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2009_CMA_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 CMA Awards">2009 CMA Awards</a>, she received two nominations and co-hosted the ceremony with Brad Paisley.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Underwood was nominated for six Academy of Country Music Awards. At the show, Underwood was named Entertainer of the Year, making her the first woman to win this award twice.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Host <a href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire" title="Reba McEntire">Reba McEntire</a> presented Underwood with the "ACM Triple Crown Award" signifying her winning Top New Artist, Top Female Vocalist, and Entertainer of the Year during her career. She was only the second Female to win the coveted "Triple Crown Award", the first being <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Mandrell" title="Barbara Mandrell">Barbara Mandrell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>, Underwood walked away with Video of the Year for "<a href="/wiki/Cowboy_Casanova" title="Cowboy Casanova">Cowboy Casanova</a>" and also won CMT Performance of the Year for "<a href="/wiki/Temporary_Home" title="Temporary Home">Temporary Home</a>" from CMT: Invitation Only presents Carrie Underwood.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Underwood won two international awards at the 8th French Country Music Awards, which were Best Female Vocalist and Video of the Year, for "Cowboy Casanova".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> At the 2010 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, she won "Favorite Country Album", for "<a href="/wiki/Play_On_(Carrie_Underwood_album)" title="Play On (Carrie Underwood album)">Play On</a>", making her the only artist in the American Music Award history to have all albums awarded in such a category.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> She co-hosted the 2010 <a href="/wiki/CMA_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="CMA Awards">CMA Awards</a> with Brad Paisley for the third year in a row. At the 2011 Grammy Awards, Underwood was nominated for 'Best Female Country Vocal Performance' for "<a href="/wiki/Temporary_Home" title="Temporary Home">Temporary Home</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Underwood was honored by the <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Television">CMT</a> Artists of the Year special as one of the 5 top Artists of the year in 2010 in country music.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The event aired on CMT on December 3, 2010. At the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> Awards, Underwood sang with <a href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler" title="Steven Tyler">Steven Tyler</a> both her song "Undo It" and <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Walk_This_Way" title="Walk This Way">Walk This Way</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2011, Underwood was one of the seven women to be honored by the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> at the <i>Girls' Night Out: Superstar Women of Country</i> special. She was recognized for being the first and only female artist in the Academy's history to ever win Entertainer of the Year twice.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> At the ceremony, <a href="/wiki/Vince_Gill" title="Vince Gill">Vince Gill</a> introduced Underwood and presented her with the special award. He sang one of her hits, "Jesus, Take The Wheel", and joined Underwood on a rendition performance of "<a href="/wiki/How_Great_Thou_Art_(hymn)" class="mw-redirect" title="How Great Thou Art (hymn)">How Great Thou Art</a>". The video of the performance turned into a <a href="/wiki/Viral_video" title="Viral video">viral sensation</a>, reaching 3 million views on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> within two days.<sup id="cite_ref-new.music.yahoo.com_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new.music.yahoo.com-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_5_(5694826253).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Carrie_Underwood_5_%285694826253%29.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood_5_%285694826253%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Carrie_Underwood_5_%285694826253%29.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood_5_%285694826253%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Carrie_Underwood_5_%285694826253%29.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood_5_%285694826253%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1122" data-file-height="1136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_5_(5694826253).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performing at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a>, in April 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In December 2009, <i>Some Hearts</i> was named the number-one Country Album of the 2000 Decade by <i>Billboard</i> and Underwood was the top-ranked female artist on <i>Billboard</i>'s Best Country Artists of the 2000 Decade list.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Overall, she was ranked No. 50 on the Artists of the Decade list by <i>Billboard</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Also in late 2009, Underwood had her very own <i><a href="/wiki/CMT_Invitation_Only" title="CMT Invitation Only">CMT Invitation Only</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> and also hosted a Christmas special, <i>Carrie Underwood: An All-Star Holiday Special</i>, a two-hour variety show on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> that featured <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a> (with whom she sang a rendition duet of "<a href="/wiki/I_Will_Always_Love_You" title="I Will Always Love You">I Will Always Love You</a>") season seven <i>American Idol</i> champion <a href="/wiki/David_Cook_(singer)" title="David Cook (singer)">David Cook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Chenoweth" title="Kristin Chenoweth">Kristin Chenoweth</a>, Brad Paisley and others.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> In May 2010, Underwood was selected on People Magazine's 100 Most Beautiful People List for 2010. This was the 4th year in a row that she was selected for the list.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Also in May, <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret" title="Victoria&#39;s Secret">Victoria's Secret</a> named her legs the Sexiest Legs in Hollywood.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In June 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine ranked Underwood as the No. 11 Queen of Pop, based on a lot of criteria from 2009 until 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Underwood co-wrote and recorded a song titled "<a href="/wiki/There%27s_a_Place_for_Us_(song)" title="There&#39;s a Place for Us (song)">There's a Place for Us</a>", the lead single from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronicles_of_Narnia:_The_Voyage_of_the_Dawn_Treader" title="The Chronicles of Narnia: The Voyage of the Dawn Treader">The Chronicles of Narnia: The Voyage of the Dawn Treader</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Underwood and songwriters, David Hodges and Hillary Lindsey, received a nomination for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song">Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In March 2011, Underwood sang <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Instant_Karma!" title="Instant Karma!">Instant Karma!</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s special <i>All Together Now – A Celebration of Service</i>, which honored former President <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_10)" title="American Idol (season 10)">season ten</a> finale of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a>,</i> Underwood selected a song for contestant <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Alaina" title="Lauren Alaina">Lauren Alaina</a> to sing.<sup id="cite_ref-content.usatoday.com_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-content.usatoday.com-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood is featured on "<a href="/wiki/Remind_Me_(Brad_Paisley_and_Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Remind Me (Brad Paisley and Carrie Underwood song)">Remind Me</a>", a duet with Brad Paisley that reached No. 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Country Songs, giving Underwood her eleventh number-one single on such chart and fourteenth overall. She has also a duet with <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a> on his 2011 album <i><a href="/wiki/Duets_II_(Tony_Bennett_album)" title="Duets II (Tony Bennett album)">Duets II</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and another duet with Randy Travis on his 2011 <i>Anniversary Celebration</i> album. Underwood was one of the headliners of the <a href="/wiki/Iheartradio" class="mw-redirect" title="Iheartradio">iHeartRadio</a> Music Festival. The event took place on September 23 and 24, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 19, Underwood performed "<a href="/wiki/You_Really_Got_a_Hold_on_Me" class="mw-redirect" title="You Really Got a Hold on Me">You Really Got a Hold on Me</a>" in order to honor <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Robinson" title="Smokey Robinson">Smokey Robinson</a>, as he was presented with the Ella Award at the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Singers" title="Society of Singers">Society of Singers</a> annual dinner. Robinson returned the favor to Underwood by singing "<a href="/wiki/My_Girl_(The_Temptations_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="My Girl (The Temptations song)">My Girl</a>" to her. At the same event, they sang together with <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Cole" title="Natalie Cole">Natalie Cole</a> and other artists a medley of multiple songs.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Underwood was reported by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> to have earned over $13 million from May 2009 to May 2010, being the top-earning <i>Idol</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-http_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In July 2011, Forbes reported that Underwood earned over $20 million between May 2010 and May 2011, being the top-earning <i>American Idol</i> alumnus for the fourth consecutive year.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> She earned $5 million between 2011 and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 4, 2012, Underwood joined <a href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler" title="Steven Tyler">Steven Tyler</a> to record <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Television">CMT's</a> <a href="/wiki/CMT_Crossroads" title="CMT Crossroads"><i>Crossroads</i></a> at the Pepsi Coliseum during the Pepsi Super Bowl Fan Jam of <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jan20_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jan20-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> It was the highest-rated episode in seven years.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 12, 2012, Underwood and Tony Bennett performed their duet "<a href="/wiki/It_Had_to_Be_You_(song)" title="It Had to Be You (song)">It Had to Be You</a>" at the 54th Annual <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> They also sang the song on the season two premiere of <a href="/wiki/Blue_Bloods_(TV_series)" title="Blue Bloods (TV series)">Blue Bloods</a> in September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Blue_Bloods_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Blue_Bloods-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932013:_Blown_Away_and_global_tour"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2013:_Blown_Away_and_global_tour">2012–2013: <i>Blown Away</i> and global tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2012–2013: Blown Away and global tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_2,_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Carrie_Underwood_2%2C_2012.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood_2%2C_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Carrie_Underwood_2%2C_2012.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood_2%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Carrie_Underwood_2%2C_2012.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood_2%2C_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1489" data-file-height="1870" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_2,_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood at <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, May 2012</div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_(album)" title="Blown Away (album)">Blown Away</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Underwood's fourth album, was released on May 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Underwood has said that this album features songs with a "darker storyline".<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> "Blown Away" debuted at No. 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, the Country Albums Chart and the Digital Albums chart in the US, selling more than 267,000 in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The first single, "<a href="/wiki/Good_Girl_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Good Girl (Carrie Underwood song)">Good Girl</a>", was released on February 23, 2012. It was officially released to Country radio on February 27, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The music video for "Good Girl" premiered on <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Tonight" title="Entertainment Tonight">Entertainment Tonight</a></i> and on <i><a href="/wiki/VEVO" class="mw-redirect" title="VEVO">VEVO</a></i> on March 12, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The song peaked at No. 1 on the Hot Country Songs chart, giving Underwood her twelfth number-one on the chart,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> and was certified Double Platinum and has sold over two million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-carrieunderwoodofficial.com_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carrieunderwoodofficial.com-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The song "<a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Blown Away (Carrie Underwood song)">Blown Away</a>" was released as the second single from the album on July 9, 2012. It was a massive success, selling over 2 million copies, being certified Triple Platinum, reaching the Top 20 of the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, the number-one spot on the <a href="/wiki/Country_Airplay" title="Country Airplay">Billboard Country Airplay</a> and the Top 2 of the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs">Top Country Songs</a>, where it became Underwood's 16th Top 10 hit on Hot Country Songs chart, a record among women in the tally's 68-year history.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The album was the 7th best-selling album of 2012, the second best-selling country album of the year and the second best-selling release by a female artist in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> It has been certified Double Platinum by the RIAA and sold over 1.7 million copies in the United States alone.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Underwood had her very own <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> Unplugged (called "VH1 Presents: Carrie Underwood Unplugged") and VH1 <a href="/wiki/Behind_The_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Behind The Music">Behind The Music</a> episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Two_Black_Cadillacs" title="Two Black Cadillacs">Two Black Cadillacs</a>", the third single from the album, was released on November 26. It became Underwood's 17th top 10 hit on the Billboard Hot Country Songs, extending her own record, later peaking at No. 2 on Billboard's Country Airplay chart and certified Platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa.com-2_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa.com-2-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In March 2013, "<a href="/wiki/See_You_Again_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="See You Again (Carrie Underwood song)">See You Again</a>" was released as the album's fourth single; it has peaked at number 2 on Country Airplay chart and has been certified Platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 2012 <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>, Underwood won the awards for Video of the Year, for "Good Girl", and Collaborative Video of the Year, for "Remind Me", her duet with Brad Paisley. She also performed "Good Girl" at the ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> At the 2012 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, she won the award for Favorite Album – Country, for <i>Blown Away</i>, and performed "Two Black Cadillacs". In early 2013, Underwood won the prize for Top Selling International Album of the Year at the 41st <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Awards_of_Australia" title="Country Music Awards of Australia">Country Music Awards of Australia</a>, held by the <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_of_Australia" title="Country Music Association of Australia">Country Music Association of Australia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Also in February 2013, Underwood won her sixth <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Country_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Country Solo Performance">Best Country Solo Performance</a>, for "Blown Away".<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> She performed a medley of "Blown Away" and "Two Black Cadillacs" at the awards show. On February 13, Underwood received two nominations for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards" title="Academy of Country Music Awards">Academy of Country Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> She won International Album of the Year at the 2013 British Country Music Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_British_Country_Music_Awards_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_British_Country_Music_Awards-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> At the 2013 <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>, Underwood won her 10th award, becoming the most awarded artist ever in CMT Music Awards history. She won Video of the Year for "Blown Away" for the fourth time, which also makes her the artist with the most wins ever in the category.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> 
During the ceremony, she paid tribute to tornado victims in Oklahoma, by performing "See You Again" backed by a choir from Nashville's Christ Church.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
