<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG/220px-Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG/330px-Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG/440px-Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2604" data-file-height="3472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_on_her_%22Blown_Away_Tour%22.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performing in Canada, during the <a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_Tour" title="Blown Away Tour">Blown Away World Tour</a>, 2012</div></div></div>
<p>In 2012, the first leg of the <i><a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_Tour" title="Blown Away Tour">Blown Away Tour</a></i> started at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> on June 21, 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> which sold out in 90 minutes,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> and five shows in Australia, including a sold-out date at the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Opera_House" title="Sydney Opera House">Sydney Opera House</a>, on July 2.<sup id="cite_ref-carrieunderwoodofficial.com_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carrieunderwoodofficial.com-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The first leg of the <i>Blown Away Tour</i> made Underwood the best-selling female country touring artist of 2012, grossing over $29.2 million and bringing her career tour revenues to over $95 million.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The tour had its own exhibition at the <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Hall of Fame">Country Music Hall of Fame</a>, called "Carrie Underwood: The Blown Away Tour Exhibition", which ran from June 5 through November 10, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The second leg of the tour started in February 2013, with shows in Ireland, an additional show in England, as part of the <a href="/wiki/C2C:_Country_to_Country" title="C2C: Country to Country">C2C: Country to Country</a> festival,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> and several shows in North America. All dates of the second leg of the <i>Blown Away Tour</i> were sold out, breaking records.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Underwood wrapped the <i>Blown Away Tour</i> in late May 2013, playing to one million fans across three continents and six countries. Her three headline arena tours have played to over 3.2 million fans combined.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Underwood released <i>The Blown Away Tour: LIVE</i>, a DVD with nearly 100 minutes of performance footage, behind-the-scene looks, interviews, and music videos from the album <i>Blown Away</i>. The DVD was released on August 13, 2013, and is Underwood's first official DVD concert.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 22, 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> ranked Underwood as the 16th money maker for the period from February 2012 to February 2013. She earned close to $12 million, being <i>American Idol</i>'s Top Earner and second for female country artists.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In June 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> placed Underwood at No. 46 on The Celebrity 100 list, reporting that she earned more than $31 million between June 2012 and June 2013, being the top-earning <i>American Idol</i>, and also being one of the ten hightest-paid women in music of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_2013_Celebrity_100_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_2013_Celebrity_100-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 21, 2013, "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Stop_Lovin%27_You_(Aerosmith_song)" title="Can&#39;t Stop Lovin&#39; You (Aerosmith song)">Can't Stop Lovin' You</a>", a song by <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a> with featured vocals by Underwood, was released as a single.<sup id="cite_ref-All_Access_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-All_Access-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 25, Underwood joined <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> onstage during the stop of the band's <a href="/wiki/50_and_Counting_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="50 and Counting Tour">50 and Counting Tour</a> in Toronto, Ontario, Canada. They performed "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Only_Rock_%27n_Roll_(But_I_Like_It)" title="It&#39;s Only Rock &#39;n Roll (But I Like It)">It's Only Rock 'n Roll (But I Like It)</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> On September 22, 2013, at the <a href="/wiki/65th_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="65th Primetime Emmy Awards">65th Primetime Emmy Awards</a>, she was part of the Emmy Awards' special tribute honoring the 50th Anniversary of 1963 Television Milestones, which includes the assassination coverage of President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>' first US appearance. She performed one of The Beatles' iconic songs, "<a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(Beatles_song)" title="Yesterday (Beatles song)">Yesterday</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932015:_Greatest_Hits:_Decade_.231"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–2015:_Greatest_Hits:_Decade_#1">2014–2015: <i>Greatest Hits: Decade #1</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2014–2015: Greatest Hits: Decade #1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1897" data-file-height="2845" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood, pregnant, at the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ole_Opry" title="Grand Ole Opry">Grand Ole Opry</a>, December 2014</div></div></div>
<p>Underwood confirmed that she began planning a new album in August 2013 and would start prep work sometime in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Underwood told <i>Billboard</i>, "After <i>The Sound of Music</i>, I feel like I can really buckle down and start working on the next album." Underwood also stated she has been planning another tour, which might be toned down from her earlier ones, stating, "I haven't thought about it much because I don't know what the next album is going to sound like, but I like just standing there and singing, too. I may take a different approach, a more simple approach on the next one. I loved the energy that rock concerts had," Underwood told <i>Billboard</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Underwood is featured on <a href="/wiki/Miranda_Lambert" title="Miranda Lambert">Miranda Lambert</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Platinum_(Miranda_Lambert_album)" title="Platinum (Miranda Lambert album)">Platinum</a></i>, on a song called "<a href="/wiki/Somethin%27_Bad" title="Somethin&#39; Bad">Somethin' Bad</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Country_Weekly_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Country_Weekly-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Released as a single, "Somethin' Bad" reached No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs">Hot Country Songs</a> chart, becoming Underwood's 13th number-one on the chart. The same week, the song vaulted to No. 19 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gary_Trust_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gary_Trust-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2014, she performed on the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_Induction_Ceremony" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame Induction Ceremony">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame Induction Ceremony</a>, paying tribute to <a href="/wiki/Linda_Ronstadt" title="Linda Ronstadt">Linda Ronstadt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Her performances were highly acclaimed by critics and even by <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Nicks" title="Stevie Nicks">Stevie Nicks</a>, who performed with Underwood.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> In September, Underwood headlined the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Global_Citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Citizen">Global Citizen</a> Festival, alongside <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/No_Doubt" title="No Doubt">No Doubt</a> and other music acts.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Her cover of <a href="/wiki/R.E.M." title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Everybody_Hurts" title="Everybody Hurts">Everybody Hurts</a>" during her performance was highly praised.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> She headlined the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Valor" class="mw-redirect" title="Concert for Valor">Concert for Valor</a> in November, alongside <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a>, and other music acts, where she was backed by the Singing Sergeants of the US Air Force during the performance of "Something in the Water".<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Underwood was asked by <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">Bono</a> himself to front <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>'s World AIDS Day (RED) Concert, alongside U2, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>'s Chris Martin, and <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, on December 1, 2014. She was joined on stage by U2 guitarist <a href="/wiki/The_Edge" title="The Edge">The Edge</a> during a performance of her song "Change", which received acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> awarded Underwood the Gene Weed Special Achievement Award, for her widespread exposure through  <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sunday_Night_Football" title="NBC Sunday Night Football">Sunday Night Football</a>, the live NBC broadcast of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music_Live!" title="The Sound of Music Live!">The Sound of Music Live!</a></i>, her worldwide <a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_Tour" title="Blown Away Tour">Blown Away Tour</a> and her charity work with the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> and her C.A.T.S. Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2014 Billboard Music Awards">2014 Billboard Music Awards</a>, Underwood won the Milestone Award, for which she had been nominated due to her chart success, especially her record of having the best starting run ever by a woman on the Country Airplay chart (18 top ten hits on the chart).<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> listed Underwood as one of the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100 most influential people in the world</a>, placing her in the "Icons" category.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> She won the award for Favorite Female Country Artist at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2014" title="American Music Awards of 2014">American Music Awards</a>, marking her eighth career AMA.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> She was named 2014's top female Christian artist by <i>Billboard</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 at the <a href="/wiki/57th_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="57th Grammy Awards">57th Grammy Awards</a>, Underwood won <a href="/wiki/Best_Country_Solo_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Country Solo Performance">Best Country Solo Performance</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Something_in_the_Water_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Something in the Water (Carrie Underwood song)">Something in the Water</a>", marking her seventh career Grammy Award.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_official_Grammy_source_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_official_Grammy_source-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2015_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2015 Billboard Music Awards">2015 Billboard Music Awards</a>, she won the award for Top Christian Song for "Something in the Water".<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> At the 2015 <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>, Underwood won three awards, including Video of the Year for "Something in the Water".<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> She won her ninth <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="American Music Award">American Music Award</a> in 2015, winning Favorite Female Country Artist.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood's first greatest hits compilation, <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits:_Decade_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Greatest Hits: Decade 1">Greatest Hits: Decade #1</a></i>, was released on December 9.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The album's lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Something_in_the_Water_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Something in the Water (Carrie Underwood song)">Something in the Water</a>", became a <a href="/wiki/Crossover_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crossover (music)">crossover</a> success. It reached No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs">Hot Country Songs</a> chart, becoming her fourteenth number-one hit on that chart and her second in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Wade_Jessen_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wade_Jessen-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> With fourteen number ones, she holds the record as the female country artist with the most number-one hits on the Hot Country Songs chart in the Nielsen SoundScan era (since 1991) in the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Book of World Records">Guinness Book</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-guinnessworldrecords1_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guinnessworldrecords1-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> The song topped the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Christian_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Christian Songs">Hot Christian Songs</a> chart and has held the top spot for multiple consecutive weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-Wade_Jessen_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wade_Jessen-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at No. 24 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a> chart as well.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> The song set and broke multiple <a href="/wiki/Airplay" title="Airplay">airplay</a> records on Country radio in its first week. In February 2015, "<a href="/wiki/Little_Toy_Guns" title="Little Toy Guns">Little Toy Guns</a>" was released as the second single from the compilation. The track peaked at number six on Billboard's Hot Country Songs, number two on the Country Airplay Chart and number 47 on the Hot 100. The song was nominated for Best Country Solo Performance at the 58th Grammy Awards. The compilation debuted with the biggest sales debut for a hits collection in any genre of music in more than six years and the biggest first-week sales for a female hits album in any genre in over nine years.<sup id="cite_ref-Greatest_Hits:_Decade_#1_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greatest_Hits:_Decade_#1-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> She earned $10 million between 2013 and 2014, topping Forbes' list of the top-earning <i>American Idol</i>s,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> and $8 million between 2014 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2015.E2.80.932017:_Storyteller.2C_label_change.2C_and_injury"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–2017:_Storyteller,_label_change,_and_injury">2015–2017: <i>Storyteller</i>, label change, and injury</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2015–2017: Storyteller, label change, and injury">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood returned to the studio to finish her fifth studio album in the spring of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Storyteller_(Carrie_Underwood_album)" title="Storyteller (Carrie Underwood album)">Storyteller</a></i> was released on October 23, 2015, and the lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Smoke_Break" title="Smoke Break">Smoke Break</a>" was released to radio.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> <i>Storyteller</i> debuted at No. 2 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, making Underwood the only country artist to have their first five studio albums debut at Nos. 1 or 2 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard11-2-2015_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard11-2-2015-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the album debuted at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Top Country Albums</a> chart, earning Underwood another record as the only artist to score six consecutive number-one albums on that chart.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard11-1-2015_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard11-1-2015-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>  <i>Storyteller</i> has since been certified Platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Heartbeat_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Heartbeat (Carrie Underwood song)">Heartbeat</a>", became Underwood's 14th leader on the <a href="/wiki/Country_Airplay" title="Country Airplay">Country Airplay</a> while the album's third single, "<a href="/wiki/Church_Bells_(song)" title="Church Bells (song)">Church Bells</a>", became her 15th career No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Country_Airplay" title="Country Airplay">Country Airplay</a> chart, both extending her record for the most number one's among women in the history of the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-country_airplay_record_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country_airplay_record-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Underwood became the first female artist to score two number one hits on the Country Airplay chart in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> A fourth single, "<a href="/wiki/Dirty_Laundry_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Dirty Laundry (Carrie Underwood song)">Dirty Laundry</a>", was released from the album in August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><i>Billboard</i> ranked Underwood as the top female country artist for the year, and fifth overall.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood launched the <a href="/wiki/Storyteller_Tour:_Stories_in_the_Round" title="Storyteller Tour: Stories in the Round">Storyteller Tour</a>, her fifth headlining tour, in January 2016, with a second half picking up in August. The tour has since played to over 1 million fans, completing 92 shows across 7 countries while being named by <i>Billboard</i> the top country tour for the first half of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> She earned $26 million between 2015 and 2016, raking among Forbes' list of highest-paid country music acts,<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> and $20 million between 2016 and 2017, ranking on Billboard's Top 50 Money Makers list.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2016, Underwood received three nominations from the CMT Music Awards, taking home two honors for "Smoke Break", expanding her <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="CMT Music Award">CMT Music Award</a> total to 15—the most among all acts.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> She was named Female Vocalist of the Year by the <a href="/wiki/American_Country_Countdown_Awards" title="American Country Countdown Awards">American Country Countdown Awards</a> in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> and also received the <a href="/wiki/CMA_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="CMA Award">CMA</a> Chairman's Award.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> In July, she picked up her fifth <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Award</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Award_for_Choice_Music_%E2%80%93_Country_Artist" title="Teen Choice Award for Choice Music – Country Artist">Choice Country Artist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Underwood also received two nominations from the Billboard Music Awards, including Top Country Artist.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> In September 2016, Underwood was the first artist to receive the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards" title="Academy of Country Music Awards">ACM</a> Lifting Lives Gary Haber Award, for her continuous work with charities.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 20, 2016, Underwood was honored as one of <a href="/wiki/CMT_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="CMT (U.S. TV channel)">CMT</a> Artists of the Year, marking her third year to receive the award.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Underwood received four nominations for the 50th annual <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="Country Music Association Awards">Country Music Association Awards</a>, including her first nomination for Entertainer of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> She walked away with Female Vocalist of the Year, her fourth time to win the award.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> She further received three nominations for the 2016 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>, including the top prize for Artist of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> She won <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award_for_Favorite_Country_Female_Artist" title="American Music Award for Favorite Country Female Artist">Favorite Female Country Artist</a> for the fourth time and Favorite Country Album (for <i>Storyteller</i>) for the fifth time, expanding her record as the only artist to win the award for all albums released.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood was one of 30 artists to perform on "<i><a href="/wiki/Forever_Country" title="Forever Country">Forever Country</a></i>", a mash-up track of "<a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Home,_Country_Roads" title="Take Me Home, Country Roads">Take Me Home, Country Roads</a>", "<a href="/wiki/On_the_Road_Again_(Willie_Nelson_song)" title="On the Road Again (Willie Nelson song)">On the Road Again</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/I_Will_Always_Love_You" title="I Will Always Love You">I Will Always Love You</a>" celebrating 50 years of the <a href="/wiki/CMA_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="CMA Awards">CMA Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> The single debuted at number one on Billboard's <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs">Hot Country Songs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016, she joined <a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a> for a series of concerts in Australia and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2017, she received her ninth <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People&#39;s Choice Awards">People's Choice</a> award, winning Favorite Female Country Artist.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Underwood received one nomination – <a href="/wiki/Best_Country_Solo_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Country Solo Performance">Best Country Solo Performance</a> – for her single "Church Bells" for the 59th annual <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> awards.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> She and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a> performed their new single, "<a href="/wiki/The_Fighter_(Keith_Urban_song)" title="The Fighter (Keith Urban song)">The Fighter</a>," at the Grammy ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>  Their joint single peaked in the top two of the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs">Hot Country Songs</a> and top twenty of the <a href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary" class="mw-redirect" title="Adult contemporary">adult contemporary</a> chart and was certified platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She received two nominations for the 52nd annual <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> Awards, including Entertainer of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> She scored three more nominations for the 2017 <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a> in June, including Video of the Year for "Church Bells."<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> She won Female Video of the year, extending her record for most wins in the show's history.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> Underwood scored two nominations for the 2017 Teen Choice awards, including Choice Country Artist,
which she won for a third consecutive year.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> She received one nomination from the 45th annual <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award_for_Favorite_Country_Female_Artist" title="American Music Award for Favorite Country Female Artist">Favorite Female Artist – Country</a> category, which she won for the fourth year in a row, bringing her total to twelve American Music awards.
</p><p>In January 2017, Underwood took time off at the beginning of the year to spend time with family, and would then, possibly, begin to write for her next album.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> In March 2017, Underwood signed with <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records_Nashville" title="Capitol Records Nashville">Capitol Records Nashville</a> after being with Arista Nashville for nearly twelve years.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> unveiled a new figure of Underwood when the Nashville location opened in April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Matthew_West" title="Matthew West">Matthew West</a> collaborated with Underwood, who performed background vocals on the song "Something Greater" from his album, <i>All In</i> (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> Underwood and Brad Paisley hosted the CMA Awards in November, marking their 10th consecutive year as hosts.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Underwood again received a nomination in the Female Vocalist category, her twelfth nomination to date.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> She performed "<a href="/wiki/Softly_and_Tenderly" title="Softly and Tenderly">Softly and Tenderly</a>" as part of a tribute to the victims of the Route 91 Harvest Music Festival shooting, and the performance received widespread acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood released her second concert experience, <i>The Storyteller Tour: Live from Madison Square Garden,</i> on November 17.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> A few days after the <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="Country Music Association Awards">CMA Awards</a> in November 2017, Underwood sustained injuries in a fall at home that resulted in a broken wrist and several facial stitches. Underwood did not make any public appearances for several months following the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.93present:_Cry_Pretty"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–present:_Cry_Pretty">2018–present: <i>Cry Pretty</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2018–present: Cry Pretty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood,_Grand_Ole_Opry_House,_Nashville,_TN,_June_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0e/Carrie_Underwood%2C_Grand_Ole_Opry_House%2C_Nashville%2C_TN%2C_June_2018.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood%2C_Grand_Ole_Opry_House%2C_Nashville%2C_TN%2C_June_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0e/Carrie_Underwood%2C_Grand_Ole_Opry_House%2C_Nashville%2C_TN%2C_June_2018.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood%2C_Grand_Ole_Opry_House%2C_Nashville%2C_TN%2C_June_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0e/Carrie_Underwood%2C_Grand_Ole_Opry_House%2C_Nashville%2C_TN%2C_June_2018.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood%2C_Grand_Ole_Opry_House%2C_Nashville%2C_TN%2C_June_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1563" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood,_Grand_Ole_Opry_House,_Nashville,_TN,_June_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood at the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ole_Opry" title="Grand Ole Opry">Grand Ole Opry</a>, June 2018</div></div></div>
<p>In January 2018, Underwood released "<a href="/wiki/The_Champion_(song)" title="The Champion (song)">The Champion</a>", a promotional duet single featuring <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a> for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LII" title="Super Bowl LII">Super Bowl LII</a>. "The Champion" is Underwood's first under the pop genre. The song debuted at number 47 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, powered by its launch at number three on the Digital Song Sales chart with 61,000 downloads.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood met songwriter/producer <a href="/wiki/David_Garcia_(musician)" title="David Garcia (musician)">David Garcia</a> in 2017, with whom she began co-producing her new album.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie&#39;s_Letter_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie&#39;s_Letter-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Underwood returned to the stage for the first time since her accident and debuted her new single "<a href="/wiki/Cry_Pretty_(song)" title="Cry Pretty (song)">Cry Pretty</a>" at the 53rd Annual <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards" title="Academy of Country Music Awards">ACM Awards</a> on April 15, where she received two nominations; she won the award for Vocal Event of the Year for "The Fighter" with Keith Urban.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 11, she celebrated a decade of being an <a href="/wiki/Opry" class="mw-redirect" title="Opry">Opry</a> member.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> On May 13, Underwood returned to <i>American Idol</i>, now rebooted on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>, to mentor the top five of the season sixteen contestants. She performed "Cry Pretty", in addition to "See You Again" with the remaining top five contestants.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 8, Underwood received four nominations and one win for the 2018 <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>. She performed “Cry Pretty” at the ceremony in June and expanded her record as the artist with the most wins in the show's history.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> She received a nomination for <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Award_for_Choice_Music_%E2%80%93_Country_Artist" title="Teen Choice Award for Choice Music – Country Artist">Choice Country Artist</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Cry_Pretty_(song)" title="Cry Pretty (song)">Cry Pretty</a>" received a nomination for Choice Country Song for the Teen Choice awards, winning Choice Country Artist and expanding her record for most wins in the category.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> On June 22, Underwood was honored with the Hero award from the Radio Disney Music Awards, in recognition of her humanitarian efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> She and <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a> performed their song "The Champion" together at the awards ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Her sixth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Cry_Pretty" title="Cry Pretty">Cry Pretty</a></i>, was released on September 14, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> The same week, the album's second single was confirmed to be “<a href="/wiki/Love_Wins_(song)" title="Love Wins (song)">Love Wins</a>”, with the music video debuting on September 11.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1350" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_Cry_Pretty_Tour_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performs during the <i>Cry Pretty</i> tour, May 2019.</div></div></div>
<p><i>Cry Pretty</i> debuted at number one in over 20 countries<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceD_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceD-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> and number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, setting several records upon arrival. Underwood is the first woman to hit the top of the Billboard 200 chart with four country albums. <i>Cry Pretty's</i> debut frame of 266,000 units is the biggest week for any album by a woman and a country album in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> This was Underwood's seventh consecutive album to debut at No. 1 on the Top Country Albums chart. <i>Cry Pretty's</i> debut week also marks the most first week streams by any female in country music.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceD_282-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceD-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> The album finished 2018 as the best-selling solo female album and the seventh best-selling album overall, with over 401,000 copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood performed "Spinning Bottles", a song from the album, at the 46th annual <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a> on October 9, also winning one award for Favorite Female Country Artist.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Brad_Paisley" title="Brad Paisley">Brad Paisley</a> and Underwood hosted the <a href="/wiki/52nd_Annual_Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="52nd Annual Country Music Association Awards">52nd Annual Country Music Association Awards</a> on November 14, 2018, where she picked up her fifth win as the CMA's Female Vocalist of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> The same month, Underwood announced she would kick off the <a href="/wiki/Cry_Pretty_Tour_360" title="Cry Pretty Tour 360">Cry Pretty Tour 360</a> in May 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> As well as five other dates in United Kingdom arenas, it was announced that the leg of the tour would include a performance at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood received one nomination - Female Artist of the Year - for the 54th <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards" title="Academy of Country Music Awards">Academy of Country Music Awards</a> taking place April 7.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> She performed with <a href="/wiki/This_Is_Us_(TV_series)" title="This Is Us (TV series)">This is Us</a> actress <a href="/wiki/Chrissy_Metz" title="Chrissy Metz">Chrissy Metz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Alaina" title="Lauren Alaina">Lauren Alaina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Guyton" title="Mickey Guyton">Mickey Guyton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maddie_%26_Tae" title="Maddie &amp; Tae">Maddie &amp; Tae</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> She gave the debut performance of "<a href="/wiki/Southbound_(Carrie_Underwood_song)" title="Southbound (Carrie Underwood song)">Southbound</a>,"the official third single from the <i>Cry Pretty</i> album, during the show.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood further received two more nominations for the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard Music Awards">Billboard Music Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award_for_Top_Country_Album" title="Billboard Music Award for Top Country Album">Top Country Album</a> for <i>Cry Pretty</i> and Top Female Country Artist, winning the latter, bringing her total career wins to 11.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the 2019 <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>, Underwood's video for "Cry Pretty" received a nomination for Video of the Year and "Love Wins" received a nomination for Female Video of the Year, with the awards airing live June 5.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> Underwood performed "Southbound" at <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Park_(Nashville)" title="Centennial Park (Nashville)">Centennial Park</a> during the show's broadcast; the performance was free and open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> “Cry Pretty” won Video of the Year and “Love Wins” won Female Video, extending Underwood's lead as the most awarded artist in the show's history, and giving her a total of 20 CMT awards.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> On June 8, the official music video for "Southbound" premiered on Underwood's YouTube channel.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 19, she returned to <a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a> to perform "Southbound" during the season's finale episode.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> On June 7, Underwood headlined the second day of CMA Music Fest in Nashville, where <a href="/wiki/Joan_Jett" title="Joan Jett">Joan Jett</a> made a surprise appearance on stage.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> In July 2019, she performed at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a>, as part of her Cry Pretty 360 Tour.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2019, Underwood will host the <a href="/wiki/53rd_Annual_Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="53rd Annual Country Music Association Awards">53rd Annual Country Music Association Awards</a> alongside Reba McEntire and Parton; it will be Underwood's 12th time hosting the show and first time hosting it without Paisley.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> Underwood is nominated for Entertainer of the Year and Female Vocalist of the Year and <i>Cry Pretty</i> is nominated for Album of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2019, Underwood was named one of the CMT Artists of the Year, her fifth time receiving the award.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Artistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice">Voice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Voice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood has been highly acclaimed for her vocal talents. <a href="/wiki/David_Wild" title="David Wild">David Wild</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> has praised her voice, saying that "she can hit any note".<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Biography_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Biography-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> Her vocal range has been described as "enormous", with critics highlighting her ability to hold notes for an extended period of time. <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> describes her vocal ability as "freakish".<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Concert critics have pointed out that "she'll let loose with an improbably long note that runs through more octaves than you knew existed".<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> When asked if it ever becomes difficult to belt at such high intensity during her 90–120 minute live shows, Underwood responded, "I'm too proud to drop keys. I won't do it. Maybe the older I get, I'll write some songs in lower keys so it'll be easier. I've always been pretty good as far as stamina onstage. Being able to work out and stay physically strong is important... So far, it's worked for me. I'm just blessed at being able to be loud for long periods of time."<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Fellow country music singer <a href="/wiki/Randy_Travis" title="Randy Travis">Randy Travis</a> paid high praises to Underwood's voice when asked about her cover of his 1988 hit song "<a href="/wiki/I_Told_You_So_(Randy_Travis_song)" title="I Told You So (Randy Travis song)">I Told You So</a>", saying that "her voice is so much better suited to the song. I have a <a href="/wiki/Baritone" title="Baritone">baritone</a> voice, and her <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a> voice really fits well with the range of the song. Her ability to get into the upper register of her voice and just hold those high notes is great."<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>  Her voice has also been praised as "versatile".<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> She has indeed performed live versions of <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a> songs like "<a href="/wiki/How_Great_Thou_Art" title="How Great Thou Art">How Great Thou Art</a>", in which <i><a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a></i> critics noticed her ability to move an audience with a "powerful performance",<sup id="cite_ref-new.music.yahoo.com_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new.music.yahoo.com-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and Rock songs like <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N&#39; Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Paradise_City" title="Paradise City">Paradise City</a>", with <i>Rolling Stone</i> critics saying it was a "standout performance", adding that "when the song reached its crescendo, the singer went right over the edge with it, twirling like a tornado and tossing in more than a few banshee wails" and even saying "if the original members of Guns N' Roses ever wanted to reunite without <a href="/wiki/Axl_Rose" title="Axl Rose">Axl Rose</a>, they might be wise to ask Carrie Underwood to fill his bandana".<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood has credited "music as a whole" as her major influence, since she "grew up listening to <i>music</i>" and "there were songs, different kind of songs coming at me from everywhere".<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> But she has occasionally mentioned <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">Rock</a> acts like <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/My_Chemical_Romance" title="My Chemical Romance">My Chemical Romance</a> as influences.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> Among <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">Country</a> artists, she has listed <a href="/wiki/George_Strait" title="George Strait">George Strait</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-YouTube_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YouTube-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Randy_Travis" title="Randy Travis">Randy Travis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Martina_McBride" title="Martina McBride">Martina McBride</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire" title="Reba McEntire">Reba McEntire</a>, and Garth Brooks as influences.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> Although never publicly mentioning <a href="/wiki/Faith_Hill" title="Faith Hill">Faith Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a> as musical influences, critics have linked Underwood's musical style to those of Hill and Twain.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> Her music is generally <a href="/wiki/Country_pop" title="Country pop">Country pop</a> with <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">Rock</a> influence similar to that of <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>, as noticed by <i>Rolling Stone</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> She has also released songs with <a href="/wiki/Christian_music" title="Christian music">Christian music</a> influence.<sup id="cite_ref-Beville_Dunkerlley_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beville_Dunkerlley-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg/220px-Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg/330px-Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg/440px-Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Underwood_Blown_Away_Tour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performing during the <a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_Tour" title="Blown Away Tour">Blown Away World Tour</a>, May 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Since her debut in 2005, Underwood has been praised by both veteran artists and music critics. <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> describes Underwood as "the female vocalist of her generation of any genre",<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine refers to her as <a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Country Music's reigning Queen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Grady Smith of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> has praised her, saying "Carrie Underwood has emerged as the leader of country music".<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> listed her in their <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100 most influential people in the world</a> in 2014, in which <a href="/wiki/Brad_Paisley" title="Brad Paisley">Brad Paisley</a> wrote "not only has she earned her place, she's also raised the bar: she's a prolific songwriter, a <a href="/wiki/Trendsetter" class="mw-redirect" title="Trendsetter">trendsetter</a> and an <a href="/wiki/List_of_Grand_Ole_Opry_Members" title="List of Grand Ole Opry Members">Opry member</a>", and further considers her to be "the best singer in any format of music."<sup id="cite_ref-Time_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vince_Gill" title="Vince Gill">Vince Gill</a> has also stated: "The possibility of Carrie's longevity is through the roof. There are fine singers, and there are gifted, great singers, and she's one of those. Her vocal skills are off the hook".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_324-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Etheridge" title="Melissa Etheridge">Melissa Etheridge</a> also adds saying "she has a power in her country music, in her singing. She can crossover to <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">Rock</a> in a second".<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Biography_305-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Biography-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> She has further received public commendation from <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Nicks" title="Stevie Nicks">Stevie Nicks</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler" title="Steven Tyler">Steven Tyler</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-YouTube_315-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YouTube-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Loretta_Lynn" title="Loretta Lynn">Loretta Lynn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Wild" title="David Wild">David Wild</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> has stated that "Carrie Underwood is the greatest thing that <i>American Idol</i> ever gave us".<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Biography_305-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Biography-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> She was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Hall_of_Fame" title="Oklahoma Hall of Fame">Oklahoma Hall of Fame</a> in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> in 2018, for her achievements in music.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood has influenced pop girl group <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Harmony" title="Fifth Harmony">Fifth Harmony</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> singer <a href="/wiki/Mollie_King" title="Mollie King">Mollie King</a> of British pop girl group <a href="/wiki/The_Saturdays" title="The Saturdays">The Saturdays</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> singer <a href="/wiki/Kelsea_Ballerini" title="Kelsea Ballerini">Kelsea Ballerini</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Voice (U.S. TV series)">The Voice</a></i> winner <a href="/wiki/Danielle_Bradbery" title="Danielle Bradbery">Danielle Bradbery</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> <i>American Idol</i> runner-up <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Alaina" title="Lauren Alaina">Lauren Alaina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> and singer and actress <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Hale" title="Lucy Hale">Lucy Hale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_achievements">Awards and achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Awards and achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Carrie_Underwood" title="List of awards and nominations received by Carrie Underwood">List of awards and nominations received by Carrie Underwood</a></div>
<p>Underwood has been the recipient of seven <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_official_Grammy_source_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_official_Grammy_source-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> eleven <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard Music Awards">Billboard Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> fourteen <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards" title="Academy of Country Music Awards">Academy of Country Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> thirteen <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> nine <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="Country Music Association Awards">Country Music Association Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> seven <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Awards</a>, five <a href="/wiki/CMT_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="CMT (U.S. TV channel)">CMT</a> Artists of the Year awards,<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> and twenty <a href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Awards" title="CMT Music Awards">CMT Music Awards</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> As a songwriter, she has also received a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> nomination<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> and won ten <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music,_Inc." title="Broadcast Music, Inc.">BMI Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> Underwood was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ole_Opry" title="Grand Ole Opry">Grand Ole Opry</a> in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> for her many accomplishments in country music, and into the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Oklahoma Music Hall of Fame">Oklahoma Music Hall of Fame</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> She was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Hall_of_Fame" title="Oklahoma Hall of Fame">Oklahoma Hall of Fame</a> in 2017, the highest honor one can receive from the state. In December 2009, she was awarded the prestigious Harmony Award from the <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Symphony_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Nashville Symphony Orchestra">Nashville Symphony Orchestra</a> for her achievements in music across many genres.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, she received Artist Achievement Award at the 38th Annual New York Honors Gala held by the <a href="/wiki/T.J._Martell_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="T.J. Martell Foundation">T.J. Martell Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, she was honored by the <a href="/wiki/Country_Radio_Broadcasters" title="Country Radio Broadcasters">Country Radio Broadcasters</a>' Board of Directors with the CRB Artist Humanitarian Award at the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Country_Radio_Seminar" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Radio Seminar">Country Radio Seminar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Regarded as one of the most successful artists in any musical genre,<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Underwood has sold 70 million records worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> In the US, she has sold 16.3 million albums<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> making her the best-selling album artist of the <i>American Idol</i> franchise, with <i>Billboard</i> calling her the ultimate <i>Idol</i> success story.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> has declared Underwood the most successful American Idol winner of all time, with more albums sold and more revenue generated than any of the other contestants in the show's 15 seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> Underwood had a fast commercial impact on the music industry, with her debut album, <i>Some Hearts</i>, becoming the fastest-selling debut country album in the history of the <a href="/wiki/SoundScan" class="mw-redirect" title="SoundScan">SoundScan</a> era,<sup id="cite_ref-cmt20070110_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmt20070110-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cst_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cst-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> the best-selling solo female debut album in country music history,<sup id="cite_ref-Gactv.com_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gactv.com-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> the best-selling Country album of the last 14 years,<sup id="cite_ref-Grein_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grein-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and the best-selling album by an American Idol alum in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> With her debut single, "Inside Your Heaven", she also broke <i>Billboard</i> chart history as the first country music artist ever to debut at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a> and the song became the first song from a country artist to go to No. 1 on the Hot 100 since country group <a href="/wiki/Lonestar" title="Lonestar">Lonestar</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Amazed" title="Amazed">Amazed</a>" did so in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-PRNewswire_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRNewswire-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> "Inside Your Heaven" is the only single by a solo country artist in the 2000 decade to reach No. 1 on the Hot 100 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> With the singles from her second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Carnival_Ride" title="Carnival Ride">Carnival Ride</a></i>, she became the first female country artist since <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a> in 1995 to pull four number-one's from one album.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, with the singles of her third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Play_On_(Carrie_Underwood_album)" title="Play On (Carrie Underwood album)">Play On</a></i>, she achieved ten career number-one singles on the Hot Country Songs, an achievement for which she was named by the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Book of World Records">Guinness Book of World Records</a></i> as the female country artist with the most number-one hits on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs">Hot Country Songs</a> chart (since accurate sales records were introduced in the US in 1991), tied with <a href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire" title="Reba McEntire">Reba McEntire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guinnessworldrecords1_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guinnessworldrecords1-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> With such a feat, she became the only female artist in country music history to have eleven consecutive top two singles; at that time, she had twelve official country singles: ten number-ones. She also became the first woman to score ten number-ones on such a chart since <a href="/wiki/Rosanne_Cash" title="Rosanne Cash">Rosanne Cash</a> in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> She then broke and expanded her <i>Guinness Book</i> record by scoring four more number-one singles on the Hot Country Songs between 2011 and 2014, for a total of fourteen number-ones.<sup id="cite_ref-Wade_Jessen_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wade_Jessen-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> She is also the woman with the most number-ones in the history of the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Country_Airplay" title="Country Airplay">Country Airplay</a> chart, having had 15 leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-country_airplay_record_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country_airplay_record-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood's first twenty-seven singles promoted to country radio all reached the top 10 of both the Hot Country Songs and Country Airplay charts, the longest streak of top ten singles by a country artist from the start of a career.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> recognizes Underwood as the third highest-certified Country Artist of all time and the seventh highest-certified female artist on its Top Artists (Digital Songs) raking,<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> with 32.5 million certified units.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> Underwood is also the highest certified Country album artist to debut in the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> Since May 2011, Underwood is the Biggest <i>American Idol</i> Earner, with, at the time of the press release, over $66 million in tour revenues, besides her records sales.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> She is the fourth biggest album seller of the past 10 years in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup> With her sixth studio album opening at number one on Billboard's Top 200 Albums chart, Underwood broke several records: she was the first woman to launch four country albums to number one there, as well as the first female country artist to top Billboard's The Artist 100 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> In September 2018, Underwood received a star on the Hollywood Walk of Fame, for her numerous achievements in music.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> Underwood is the first female artist in ACM award history to win the ACM Entertainer of the Year award twice, taking home the top honor in 2009 and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> After taking home over 20 awards from 2006 to 2019, Underwood became the most awarded artist in the history of the CMT Music Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> As of October, 2018, she has a net worth estimated at around US$200 million.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> She has been the top-earning <i>American Idol</i> alum of all time since 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Beville_Dunkerlley_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beville_Dunkerlley-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top-EarningAmerican_Idols_2013_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top-EarningAmerican_Idols_2013-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Product_endorsements">Product endorsements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Product endorsements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood has had many endorsements throughout her career. She has signed multimillion-dollar deals with <a href="/wiki/Skechers" title="Skechers">Skechers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Target_Stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Target Stores">Target</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olay" title="Olay">Olay</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPI_Products" title="OPI Products">Nicole by OPI</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hershey_Company" title="The Hershey Company">Hershey's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almay" title="Almay">Almay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dick%27s_Sporting_Goods" title="Dick&#39;s Sporting Goods">Dick's Sporting Goods</a>. In 2005, Underwood appeared in a <a href="/wiki/Skechers" title="Skechers">Skechers</a> global advertising campaign. In 2007, Underwood appeared in Target advertisements promoting her album Carnival Ride. The limited edition of the album which included a behind the scenes DVD was exclusively sold at Target.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Underwood worked with <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> for the launch of their <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> appearing in various television commercials.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_DS_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_DS-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup> That same year, Underwood became the spokesperson for <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_Water" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitamin Water">Vitamin Water</a> starring in television and magazine advertisements. Underwood also hosts a guide to a healthy lifestyle on Vitamin Water's website.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Vitamin_Water_377-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Vitamin_Water-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup>  In 2010, Underwood became the spokesperson for the <a href="/wiki/Pedigree_Petfoods" title="Pedigree Petfoods">Pedigree</a> adoption drive. In 2011, she became the first celebrity brand ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Olay" title="Olay">Olay</a> skin care. Underwood has appeared in the global advertising campaign for their facial wash.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Olay_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Olay-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2014, Underwood signed a deal with Nicole by OPI to launch 14 new nail lacquers.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> In the same month, Underwood had signed a deal to serve as <a href="/wiki/Almay" title="Almay">Almay</a>'s global brand ambassador, where she would appear in TV and print advertisements for the brand later that month.<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2015, Underwood released a fitness clothing line named CALIA by Carrie Underwood. In collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Dick%27s_Sporting_Goods" title="Dick&#39;s Sporting Goods">Dick's Sporting Goods</a>, the line features clothing that is intended to be suitable for both active and casual wear.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood established the Checotah Animal, Town, and School Foundation in 2009. The foundation helps with general causes, needs and services in the area of Checotah to directly impact the community.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Chairty_382-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Chairty-382">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup> "My hometown is extremely supportive of me and I feel blessed to be able to create something as a way of giving back; to say thank you," said Underwood.<sup id="cite_ref-CATS_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CATS-383">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_philanthropy_384-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_philanthropy-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood is a supporter of arts education.
