In 2009, Underwood's foundation "Checotah Animal, Town &amp; School Foundation" and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> foundation "ACM Lifting Lives" partnered to give students in Checotah, Oklahoma a gift valued at more than $120,000 in new instruments for their music programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Arts_385-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Arts-385">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup> Underwood held a surprise concert at a local high school and then unveiled the gifts. The instruments will be shared throughout the Checotah school district and were ordered through Yamaha Corporate Artist Affairs at a special philanthropic price.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Arts_385-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Arts-385">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup> During the 2011 holiday season, her foundation donated $350,000 to the Checotah schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Donation_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Donation-386">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood is a supporter of animal welfare. Underwood is a supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Humane_Society_of_the_United_States" title="Humane Society of the United States">Humane Society of the United States</a> (HSUS) and has done several public service announcements for the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_HSUS_387-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_HSUS-387">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup> Underwood has also done a "Protect Your Pets" <a href="/wiki/Public_service_announcement" title="Public service announcement">public service announcement</a> for <a href="/wiki/Do_Something" title="Do Something">Do Something</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_PSA_388-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_PSA-388">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Underwood became the official spokesperson for the <a href="/wiki/Pedigree_Petfoods" title="Pedigree Petfoods">Pedigree</a> adoption drive.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Pedigree_389-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Pedigree-389">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup> On March 29, 2010, Underwood and Pedigree partnered to donate $10,000 to a New York City Animal Shelter. In April 2011, Underwood opened the Happy Paws Animal Shelter in her hometown.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_Shelter_390-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_Shelter-390">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup> On January 10, 2012, it was reported but had previously been blogged by Underwood herself on her official fan-site, that the singer rescued an abandoned dog along highway.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_saves_dogs_391-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_saves_dogs-391">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood and her husband made a video for the "Do It for Daron" campaign urging young people to stop bullying.<sup id="cite_ref-Stop_Bullying_392-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stop_Bullying-392">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup> In July 2012, she publicly endorsed same-sex marriage. She told the British newspaper <i>The Independent</i>, "As a married person myself, I don't know what it's like to be told I can't marry somebody I love and want to marry," she said. "I can't imagine how that must feel. I definitely think we should all have the right to love, and love publicly, the people that we want to love." Underwood went on to say, "Our church is gay-friendly. Above all, God wanted us to love others. It's not about setting rules, or [saying] 'everyone has to be like me'. No. We're all different. That's what makes us special. We have to love each other and get on with each other. It's not up to me to judge anybody."<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood launched the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> Lifting Lives Temporary Home Fund in 2010. The Fund specifically benefits victims of the Tennessee floods of early 2010 and it was kicked off with grants that Underwood received from ACM as Entertainer of the Year. She also teamed up with Brooks and Dunn to support the new Fund by recording a <a href="/wiki/Public_Service_Announcement" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Service Announcement">Public Service Announcement</a> (PSA).<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_donation_394-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_donation-394">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood is involved with several organizations that benefit children. In January 2010, she partnered with Country Cares for St. Jude Kids visiting the <a href="/wiki/St._Jude_Children%27s_Research_Hospital" title="St. Jude Children&#39;s Research Hospital">St. Jude Children's Research Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_st_jude_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_st_jude-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> In February 2011, Underwood donated $140,125 to <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_Save_the_Children_396-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_Save_the_Children-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> This charitable initiative was inspired by the "36 cents" written in the lyrics of Underwood's album track "Change" on her album <i>Play On</i>, which addresses how even the smallest bit of spare change that one might have can add up to make a difference and help "change" the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_Save_the_Children_396-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_Save_the_Children-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood is a supporter of the <a href="/wiki/United_Service_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="United Service Organization">United Service Organization</a>, Clothes off our back, and <a href="/wiki/Habitat_For_Humanity" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitat For Humanity">Habitat For Humanity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_giving_397-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_giving-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup> To benefit <a href="/wiki/Cancer_research" title="Cancer research">cancer research</a>, in August 2008, Underwood joined <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>, and other female artists to record the song "<a href="/wiki/Just_Stand_Up!" title="Just Stand Up!">Just Stand Up!</a>" The proceeds benefited <a href="/wiki/Stand_Up_to_Cancer" title="Stand Up to Cancer">Stand Up to Cancer</a> (SU2C). As a result of their fund raising efforts, the SU2C scientific advisory committee, overseen by the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_Cancer_Research" title="American Association for Cancer Research">American Association for Cancer Research</a> was able to award $73.6 million towards novel, groundbreaking research.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_SU2C_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_SU2C-398">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup> The song peaked at No. 11 on <i>Billboard</i>'s Hot 100 Songs.
</p><p>In 2012, Underwood donated $1 of every ticket sold on the North American leg of the <a href="/wiki/Blown_Away_Tour" title="Blown Away Tour">Blown Away Tour</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Red_Cross" title="Canadian Red Cross">Canadian</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_Red_Cross_Donation_399-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_Red_Cross_Donation-399">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup> On May 24, 2013, Underwood donated $1 million in proceeds from her recent Blown Away Tour to the Red Cross for relief efforts in response to the Oklahoma tornado.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting">Acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/How_I_Met_Your_Mother" title="How I Met Your Mother">How I Met Your Mother</a></i> in March 2010. She played the role of Tiffany, a medical sales rep that forms a relationship with Ted.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> This was the second highest rated episode for season five, gaining 10.48 million viewers. Brian Zoromski of IGN gave the episode 8.5 out of 10. He was surprised how well Underwood performed in her first acting role.<sup id="cite_ref-Hooked_Review_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hooked_Review-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup> A few months earlier, she appeared in an episode of the <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Broadcasting Service">PBS</a> <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_television_series" title="Children&#39;s television series">children's television series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Sesame_Street" title="Sesame Street">Sesame Street</a></i>, performing a <a href="/wiki/Voice-over" title="Voice-over">voice-over</a> as "Carrie Underworm" a worm who sings a song about worm pride before an auto race Sesame Street is holding.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood made her film debut in <i><a href="/wiki/Soul_Surfer_(film)" title="Soul Surfer (film)">Soul Surfer</a></i> in April 2011. She played Sarah Hill, the church youth leader who helped <a href="/wiki/Bethany_Hamilton" title="Bethany Hamilton">Bethany Hamilton</a> overcome the obstacles she faced after the shark attack.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carrie_Underwood_Soul_Surfer_405-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrie_Underwood_Soul_Surfer-405">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood played <a href="/wiki/Maria_von_Trapp" title="Maria von Trapp">Maria von Trapp</a> in NBC's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music_Live!" title="The Sound of Music Live!">The Sound of Music Live!</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NBC_musical_406-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBC_musical-406">&#91;406&#93;</a></sup> The three-hour telecast aired on December 5, 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">&#91;407&#93;</a></sup> partnering NBC with the producing team of Craig Zadan and Neil Meron. "To have a star like Carrie Underwood perform Maria in <i>The Sound of Music</i>, and in such a very special and unique production, is exciting beyond words," said Ted Chapin, President of the Rodgers &amp; Hammerstein Organization. "Part of the magic of <a href="/wiki/Rodgers_and_Hammerstein" title="Rodgers and Hammerstein">Rodgers and Hammerstein</a> is how their work has adapted itself to so many different incarnations, and I am certain the fresh spirit Underwood brings to her own songs will transition into exciting versions of the classic songs we all know and love."<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">&#91;408&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_children">Marriage and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Marriage and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood began dating <a href="/wiki/NHL" class="mw-redirect" title="NHL">NHL</a> player <a href="/wiki/Mike_Fisher_(ice_hockey)" title="Mike Fisher (ice hockey)">Mike Fisher</a> after they met at one of her concerts in late 2008, and she became engaged to him in December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">&#91;409&#93;</a></sup> On July 10, 2010, Underwood and Fisher wed at The Ritz-Carlton Lodge, Reynolds Plantation in <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_Georgia" title="Greensboro, Georgia">Greensboro, Georgia</a>, with more than 250 people in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">&#91;410&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-411">&#91;411&#93;</a></sup> The couple's first son was born in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">&#91;412&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, their second son was born.<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">&#91;413&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">&#91;414&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">&#91;415&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview on <i><a href="/wiki/CBS_News_Sunday_Morning" title="CBS News Sunday Morning">CBS News Sunday Morning</a></i> on September 16, 2018, Underwood revealed she had three miscarriages in just over a year.<sup id="cite_ref-416" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-416">&#91;416&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 11, 2011, an Ottawa radio station, 105.3 <a href="/wiki/CISS-FM" title="CISS-FM">CISS-FM</a>, stated that it would ban the playing of Underwood's music because her husband, Mike Fisher, was traded to the <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Predators" title="Nashville Predators">Nashville Predators</a> the day before. Due to Underwood's fans' threats on Facebook to never tune into the radio station, the station later modified its statement. It apologized for its actions, saying that its statements were meant to be taken as a joke, as it does not play Underwood's country songs anyway, and it was its tongue-in-cheek way of wishing Fisher the best of luck in Nashville.<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">&#91;417&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-418" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-418">&#91;418&#93;</a></sup> Fisher later criticized the station saying "obviously Carrie had nothing to do with the move or the trade or anything so to imply something like that was just wrong", and noting that both he and Underwood were disappointed in the negativity that was created by the radio station.<sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">&#91;419&#93;</a></sup> Underwood was selected by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hockey_News" title="The Hockey News">The Hockey News</a></i> on its annual list of the 100 People of Power and Influence in Ice Hockey. For the 2012 list, Underwood ranked at No. 85.<sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-420">&#91;420&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, Underwood and Fisher bought a mansion on eleven acres near <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, Canada in the luxurious Spruce Ridge district. The couple later put the mansion up for sale at an asking price of $2.2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_Mansion_421-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_Mansion-421">&#91;421&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, the couple bought a cottage outside of Nashville. They use the cottage for weekend getaways. <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah</a> toured the cottage and interviewed Underwood and Fisher there for their appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/Oprah_Prime" title="Oprah Prime">Oprah's Next Chapter</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Underwood_Cottage_422-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Underwood_Cottage-422">&#91;422&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_interests">Personal interests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrie_Underwood&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Personal interests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Underwood is a practicing <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-423" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-423">&#91;423&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-424" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-424">&#91;424&#93;</a></sup>  and is also an animal lover and a <a href="/wiki/Vegan" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegan">vegan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vegan_425-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vegan-425">&#91;425&#93;</a></sup> She stopped eating meat at the age of thirteen because she could not stand the thought of eating one of her own animals. She was voted "World's Sexiest Vegetarian" by <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a><sup id="cite_ref-goveg_426-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goveg-426">&#91;426&#93;</a></sup> in 2007 for the second time, the first being in 2005 alongside <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a>, who was himself a vegetarian at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-goveg_426-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goveg-426">&#91;426&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-427" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-427">&#91;427&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_(4344823004).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_%284344823004%29.jpg/220px-Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_%284344823004%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_%284344823004%29.jpg/330px-Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_%284344823004%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_%284344823004%29.jpg/440px-Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_%284344823004%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_Bowl_44_Carrie_Underwood_(4344823004).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwood performs at <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIV" title="Super Bowl XLIV">Super Bowl XLIV</a>, February 2010</div></div></div>
<p>In a 2007 interview with PETA, Underwood stated, "Ever since I was little I loved animals [...] If you told me I could never sing again, I'd say that was horrible, but it's not my life. If you told me I could never be around animals again, I would just die."<sup id="cite_ref-428" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-428">&#91;428&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-429" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-429">&#91;429&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2013, Underwood spoke out with disapproval regarding the Tennessee "Ag Gag bill".<sup id="cite_ref-430" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-430">&#91;430&#93;</a></sup> The bill makes it a crime to videotape animal cruelty or abuse and then fail to turn in the evidence to authorities within 48 hours. This is to stop animal rights activists from accumulating enough documentation to prove that animal cruelty is routine in big agribusiness.<sup id="cite_ref-431" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-431">&#91;431&#93;</a></sup> Underwood tweeted, "Shame on TN lawmakers for passing the Ag Gag bill. If Gov. <a href="/wiki/Bill_Haslam" title="Bill Haslam">Bill Haslam</a> signs this, he needs to expect me at his front door. Who's with me?"<sup id="cite_ref-432" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-432">&#91;432&#93;</a></sup> State Rep. <a href="/wiki/Andy_Holt_(Tennessee_politician)" title="Andy Holt (Tennessee politician)">Andy Holt</a> responded to her tweet, saying, "I would say that Carrie Underwood will stick to singing, I'll stick to lawmaking."<sup id="cite_ref-433" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-433">&#91;433&#93;</a></sup> Underwood later responded via Twitter, "I should stick to singing? Wow…sorry, I'm just a tax paying citizen concerned for the safety of my family. #NoAgGag".<sup id="cite_ref-434" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-434">&#91;434&#93;</a></sup> She also tweeted Tennessee Gov. Bill Haslam, saying "Please don't sign the Ag Gag bill. Think about the welfare of the animals as well as the consumers. I'm begging you..."<sup id="cite_ref-435" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-435">&#91;435&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood has stated that she has a great interest in sports. She has participated in the annual City of Hope Celebrity Softball tournament for charity for many years. The event takes place in <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a>, and benefits research for life-threatening diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-436" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-436">&#91;436&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, she performed the "<a href="/wiki/Star-Spangled_Banner" class="mw-redirect" title="Star-Spangled Banner">Star-Spangled Banner</a>" at Game 4 of the <a href="/wiki/2005_NBA_Finals" title="2005 NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a> between the <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio_Spurs" title="San Antonio Spurs">San Antonio Spurs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Pistons" title="Detroit Pistons">Detroit Pistons</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-437" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-437">&#91;437&#93;</a></sup> and in 2006 at the <a href="/wiki/2006_NBA_All-Star_Game" title="2006 NBA All-Star Game">NBA All-Star Game</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-438" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-438">&#91;438&#93;</a></sup> She performed at <a href="/wiki/Halftime" class="mw-redirect" title="Halftime">halftime</a> of the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving Day</a> <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> game at <a href="/wiki/Texas_Stadium" title="Texas Stadium">Texas Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>, and was friends with <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> <a href="/wiki/Quarterback" title="Quarterback">quarterback</a> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Romo" title="Tony Romo">Tony Romo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-people_439-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people-439">&#91;439&#93;</a></sup> She also performed the "Star-Spangled Banner" at the <a href="/wiki/NFL_playoffs,_2005-06#NFC:_Seattle_Seahawks_34,_Carolina_Panthers_14" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL playoffs, 2005-06">NFC Championship Game</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-440" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-440">&#91;440&#93;</a></sup> as well as at the 2006 edition of <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_600" title="Coca-Cola 600">Coca-Cola 600</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-441" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-441">&#91;441&#93;</a></sup> the MLB All Star Game in Pittsburgh, and at Game 3 of the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Series" title="2007 World Series">2007 World Series</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-442" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-442">&#91;442&#93;</a></sup> On February 7, 2010, Underwood performed the National Anthem for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIV" title="Super Bowl XLIV">Super Bowl XLIV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-443" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-443">&#91;443&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Underwood performed the opening theme song for <i><a href="/wiki/NBC_Sunday_Night_Football" title="NBC Sunday Night Football">NBC Sunday Night Football</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-444" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-444">&#91;444&#93;</a></sup> Faith Hill later expressed full support for Underwood, congratulating her via <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> and stating that it was "an awesome choice" by NBC/SNF and that Underwood "will rock it".<sup id="cite_ref-445" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-445">&#91;445&#93;</a></sup> Underwood's original song was a modification of her song "<a href="/wiki/Somethin%27_Bad" title="Somethin&#39; Bad">Oh, Sunday Night</a>", but was changed to an original song, "Game On", for the <a href="/wiki/2018_NFL_season" title="2018 NFL season">2018 NFL season</a>. She sang the National Anthem for the <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Predators" title="Nashville Predators">Nashville Predators</a> prior to their victory over the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Blackhawks" title="Chicago Blackhawks">Chicago Blackhawks</a> in Game 3 of the first round of the 2017 Stanley Cup Playoffs and prior to their victory over the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Jets" title="Winnipeg Jets">Winnipeg Jets</a> in Game 2 of the second round of the 2018 Stanley Cup Playoffs.
</p>
